### Question 46: If I take a course at another university and want to transfer the credits to Fulbright, but Fulbright doesn’t have that major code, yet the course is related to a major at Fulbright, can I count it toward that major?  
### Answer: 

No, if a course taken at another university does not have an equivalent major code at Fulbright University Vietnam, it cannot be directly counted toward a major at Fulbright. Fulbright's credit transfer and exemption policies specify that a student can transfer a maximum of 64 credit hours and that these transferred credits must be equivalent to courses offered by Fulbright. This means that for a course to count toward a major at Fulbright, it must be evaluated as equivalent to a specific course or set of courses within the Fulbright curriculum. 

The process involves submitting an Application for Credit Transfer along with detailed information about the course to the Office of the Registrar. The Registrar will then coordinate with the Office of the Dean to determine if the credit or exemption is justified. 

However, if the course is not directly equivalent to a course at Fulbright, it cannot be automatically counted toward a major. Instead, it would likely be applied to general elective credits or other requirements that do not have a specific course equivalency requirement. 

Students should consult with their Academic/Major Advisor to understand how such transferred credits can best fit into their degree program at Fulbright University Vietnam. It's important to note that all courses used to fulfill major or minor requirements must be taken for a letter grade, and students can claim a maximum of 8 credits (2 courses) toward both their Exploratory and major requirements. 

In summary, while a course from another university can contribute to a student's overall credit count at Fulbright, it cannot be directly applied to a major if there is no equivalent course at Fulbright without specific approval and evaluation processes.

### Question 47: I have 112 credits from Fulbright and 16 credits from EL. Can I graduate?  
### Answer: 

To graduate with an undergraduate degree from Fulbright, a student must earn a minimum of 128 credit hours. You currently have 112 credits from Fulbright and 16 credits from the Experiential Learning Program (ELP), which totals 128 credits. Therefore, you have met the minimum requirement to graduate. The ELP credits count toward your graduation requirement, as stated in the context: "All full-time, undergraduate, degree-seeking students must complete at least 04 credits and a maximum of 12 credits under the ELP as a graduation requirement." Since you have completed the required 16 credits, you are eligible to graduate.

### Question 48: I have received an offer to attend an international conference but lack funding. What school funds can I apply for?  
### Answer: 

Fulbright University Vietnam has a student research fund which supports student’s research projects, including capstone. Students can apply for funding from this fund to cover the costs associated with attending the international conference. It is important to submit a well-structured proposal outlining the purpose of attending the conference, how it will benefit your academic and professional development, and a detailed budget of the expected expenses. Additionally, students can explore other funding opportunities offered by external organizations, such as academic associations related to the conference's field, government grants, or private scholarships. It is advisable to start the application process early and seek guidance from the university's financial aid office or academic advisors to increase the chances of securing the necessary funds.

### Question 50: In a regular semester, can I take only 2 courses? If so, how will my tuition fees be affected?  
### Answer: 

Yes, you can take only 2 courses, which is equivalent to 8 credits. However, taking fewer than 12 credits may affect your financial aid eligibility, as it could result in part-time enrollment status. Regarding tuition fees, no reduction in tuition is granted to students whose course withdrawal results in fewer than 12 academic credits. Therefore, you will still be charged the full tuition for taking 8 credits. You would need to submit a Petition for Alternative Course Load form to the Registrar's Office for approval if you wish to take fewer than 12 credits, and it must be signed by your Academic/Major Advisor. This form is necessary to ensure compliance with the university's requirements for maintaining enrollment status and financial aid eligibility.

The first period starts after 4:00 PM Friday, Week 2 to 4:00 PM Friday, Week 4. During this time, students can request to withdraw from the course without any consequence. The second period starts after 4:00 PM Friday, Week 4 to 4:00 PM Friday, Week 8. Attempted credits and a “W” grade will be recorded on the transcript for the course(s) from which students withdraw in this period. This grade does not affect a student’s GPA. In order to withdraw from a course, students need to submit the Course Withdrawal form to the Registrar’s Office, following the above timeline. </details> 

### Question 51: Can I pursue 3 majors?  
### Answer: 

No, the policy does not allow students to pursue more than two majors. Students must complete all requirements for each major they choose, and they can only double-count up to 8 credits (two courses) between any pair of majors or between a major and a minor. For example, a student can major in both A and B and minor in C with a total of 6 double-counted courses: two in A and B, two in B and C, and two in A and C. This rule does not apply to courses that are not cross-listed or tagged. Therefore, pursuing three majors would exceed the allowed limit of two majors and would not be permitted under the given policy.

Students pursuing a double major must complete all requirements for each major. ### Question 52: How can I change my major declaration?  
### Answer: 

To change your major declaration, you typically need to follow the specific procedures outlined by your university's academic regulations. Here's a general guide based on the provided contexts:

1. **Understand the Requirements**: Review the major's description and flowchart or handbook to understand the specific requirements for the major you wish to declare. This includes prerequisite courses, specific courses needed for the major, and any additional policies or requirements.

2. **Meet with a Major Coordinator**: Contact the major coordinator for the field you are interested in. They can provide you with detailed information about the major, including any additional steps you need to take.

3. **Petition Process (if necessary)**: If there are specific courses you wish to count towards your major that are not listed or cross-listed with the major, you may need to submit a petition. This petition must be approved by the major coordinator and the Dean’s Office.

4. **Formal Declaration**: Once you have met all the requirements and received approval if necessary, formally declare your major through the appropriate channels. This often involves submitting a declaration form to the Registrar's Office or the Dean’s Office.

5. **Academic Advising**: Throughout the process, it is crucial to work closely with your academic advisor to ensure you are on track to meet all degree requirements and to plan your course of study effectively.

6. **Review and Update Your Degree Audit**: After declaring your major, check your degree audit to ensure that your major has been correctly recorded and that all required courses are accounted for in your academic plan.

It's important to note that the specific steps and requirements can vary between universities, so always refer to your institution's academic catalog or consult with the Dean’s Office and academic advisors for the most accurate and up-to-date information.

Regarding the provided contexts, the Social Studies and History majors have specific requirements for declaration and completion, including gateway courses, foundational courses, and capstone projects. For Social Studies, you need to complete Social Inquiry and at least two 100 or 200-level courses to declare the major. For History, you must complete Exploring the Past and Hands-On History to declare the major, and for the minor, Exploring the Past is required.

If you are facing exceptional circumstances, such as illness or academic difficulties, you should also refer to the university's policy on exceptional circumstances and follow the appropriate procedures for requesting a change in course load or a leave of absence.

In summary, to change your major declaration, you should:

- Review the major's requirements and policies.
- Meet with the major coordinator and academic advisor.
- Submit a petition if necessary and get approval.
- Formally declare your major through the appropriate channels.
- Ensure your degree audit is updated and that you are on track to graduate.

Always refer to your university's academic catalog and consult with academic advisors for the most accurate and detailed information.

### Question 53: What is the process of delaying my payment?  
### Answer: 

To delay your tuition fee payment, you should contact Student Financial Services. Before placing a student in a payment delay, the Student Financial Services team will attempt to determine the circumstances and request a timely response from the student. If you anticipate being unable to clear the account on time, you should meet with the Student Financial Services team as soon as possible to request assistance and alternative solutions. They will work with you to understand your situation and may offer a payment plan or other assistance to help you manage your financial obligations. Remember, a student will only be reinstated as "Active" status if the outstanding balance is cleared. It is crucial to communicate your situation proactively to avoid any negative consequences such as being placed on Administrative Leave of Absence (Admin LOA) which could lead to withdrawal from the university if no action is taken or no confirmation of return is provided.

### Question 54: Which major has the fewest requirements?  
### Answer: 

The major with the fewest requirements is Art and Media Studies. It requires only the completion of the courses necessary to earn a B.A. in Art and Media Studies. Other majors, such as Engineering and Computer Science, have more structured requirements including specific core courses, mathematics or basic science courses, programming courses, capstone projects, and additional advanced-level courses. The Art and Media Studies program description emphasizes a thorough understanding of the arts in society and fosters a commitment to ongoing inquiry, innovation, and imagination through study and practice. It does not specify a minimum number of required courses beyond those needed to complete the degree, making it the major with the fewest explicit requirements listed in the provided contexts.

### Question 55: How many courses can I take in total?  
### Answer: 

The total number of courses a student can take is not explicitly limited by the given text. However, there are several constraints and limits provided:

1. **Exploratory Requirements**: Students need to complete 8 credits (2 courses) from each of three categories (E1, E2, and STEM) for a total of 24 credits (6 courses) for classes of 2025, 2026, and 2027. For class of 2024 students, it's 16 credits (4 courses).

2. **Major Requirements**: Students can claim a maximum of 8 credits (2 courses) toward both their Exploratory and major requirements.

3. **Double Major**: Students pursuing a double major must complete all requirements for each major.

4. **Double-Counting**: Up to 8 credits (2 courses) can be used to satisfy both sets of requirements (major and minor) if the courses are cross-listed or tagged.

5. **Elective Courses**: Students are free to take elective courses from the Course Catalogue, but the total number of earned credits must meet the degree requirements.

6. **Capstone Project**: Students have the option to complete an 8-credit capstone project in their major area of study or fulfill those credits with additional advanced coursework.

7. **Core Courses**: Class of 2027 and earlier students need to complete 5 core courses (20 credits).

Given these constraints, the total number of courses a student can take is not directly specified but is influenced by the need to meet these various requirements. The maximum number of courses that can be double-counted is 8 credits (2 courses), and students are encouraged to complete their Exploratory requirements by the end of their second year.

Therefore, the total number of courses a student can take is influenced by their ability to meet all these requirements while also taking advantage of elective courses to reach the total earned credits needed for their degree. The exact number will depend on the student's chosen majors, minors, and how they allocate their credits across Exploratory, major, and elective categories.

### Question 56: How many courses in a semester can I take in total?  
### Answer: 

The typical full-time course load is 16 credit hours per term or 4 courses of 4 credit hours each. Students are required to register for no fewer than 12 credit hours and no more than 20 credit hours per term. To take fewer than 12 or more than 16 credit hours in one term, students must submit a Petition for Alternative Course Load or Maximum Course Load Request form to the Registrar's Office, which must be approved and signed by the Academic/Major Advisor before submission.

### Question 57: How many courses does the university offer?  
### Answer: 

The university offers a variety of courses across different disciplines, including Signal, Systems, and Control, Computer Vision, Introduction to Machine Learning, Algorithm, Statistical Learning, Introduction to AI, Operations Research, and Introduction to Quantitative Finance, among others. Additionally, there are Pure Mathematics courses such as Abstract Algebra and Real Analysis, and research seminars that students can participate in for academic credit with advisor approval. The university also offers Exploratory requirements for students in categories like Arts and Humanities, Social Sciences, Sciences and Engineering, and Mathematics and Computing, with varying credit requirements based on the student's class year. Elective courses are available for students to complete their degree requirements, and the university also has an Experiential Learning Program (ELP) that allows students to earn academic credit through various experiential learning streams. The university uses the credit hour system, with a typical full-time course load being 16 credit hours per term, which equates to 4 courses of 4 credit hours each. Students must earn a minimum of 128 credit hours to graduate with an undergraduate degree from Fulbright University Vietnam.

STUDENT ENROLLMENT: 3.1 Course Load and Credit Hours Fulbright University Vietnam uses the “credit hour” as the quantum for course workload in the undergraduate program. A credit hour typically represents 3 hours of work during each week of a 16-week term. For a 4- credit hour course, a student would, therefore, be expected to put in 12 hours of work per week, including class time, for a total of 192 hours of work during a term. There are earned credits and attempted credits. Earned credits refer to the number of credit hours a student successfully completes with a grade of D or higher for letter grade options and a Pass for Pass/No Pass options. Attempted credits are the credit hours students enroll in and are recorded in the transcript, regardless of whether they complete the courses or pass them. This includes all courses for which a student receives a grade, including withdrawals (W), incompletes (I), repeats (RP), and failures (F). See section 4 for more details on different types of grades. To graduate

[Source: CS_major_handbook.pdf, Page: 12]
limit is independently applied to each major. Students should aim to complete the Exploratory requirements by the end of their second year. Notes: •  Class of 2023 students are exempted from the Exploratory requirements. • There are four exploratory categories for the students of classes of 2024, 2025, 2026, and 2027: E1-Arts and Humanities, E2-Social Sciences, E3- Sciences and Engineering, and E4-Mathematics and Computing. • Class of 2024 students need to complete 16 credits (4 courses) to fulﬁll their Exploratory requirements, one course from each category, with at most 4 out of 16 credits counted as Pass/No Pass. • Students of classes of 2025, 2026, and 2027 need to complete 32 credits (8 courses), eight credits from each category, to fulﬁll their Exploratory requirements. ### Question 58: How can I audit a course?  
### Answer: 

I cannot audit a course. The context provided does not mention auditing a course. It only provides information about how to dispute a final grade. The context does not mention any procedures for auditing a course, only for appealing a final grade. The Registrar's Office and the Dean's Office are involved in the grade appeal process, but there is no mention of auditing a course in this context. The only relevant action mentioned is filing a Review of Final Grade Request form within five business days if a student wishes to dispute a final grade. Therefore, based on the information provided, auditing a course is not an option described in this context.

APPEALS: A student who wishes to dispute a final grade in a course should first discuss the matter with the course instructor(s). If the matter remains unresolved and the student believes there has been an error in grading, bias, or failure to follow published grading policies, the student may file an appeal as follows: • Submit the Review of Final Grade Request form to the Registrar's Office within five (05) business days from the date on which the Registrar's Office posts the final grade for the term. • The Registrar's Office informs the Dean’s Office of the case. After investigation, if the Deans can mediate, no further action is required. Otherwise, the Registrar's Office organizes a panel review with the Dean’s Office for an independent evaluation of the grade. The grade determined after this evaluation shall be the final grade. ### Question 59: If I'm going for a double major then how many courses can be double count maximum?  
### Answer: 

The maximum number of courses that can be double-counted for a double major at Fulbright University is 8 credits (2 courses) per each pair of majors. This means that for two majors A and B, up to 8 credits (2 courses) can be used to satisfy both sets of requirements. However, this limit is per each pair of majors, and it does not restrict the total number of double-counted credits or courses a student can claim overall. For example, a student can major in both A and B and minor in C with a total of 6 double-counted courses: two in A and B, two in B and C, and two in A and C. This rule does not apply to courses that are not cross-listed or tagged.

### Question 62: Why and how am I getting academic suspension?  
### Answer: 

You are getting academic suspension because you failed to fulfill all the requirements of your Learning Contract while on Academic Probation. The process involves receiving an Academic Warning first, which requires you to attend an Academic Progress Meeting and create a Learning Contract with specific conditions. If you fail to meet these conditions, you may be placed on Academic Probation, which typically lasts for a term. If you continue to fail to meet the requirements of your Learning Contract while on Academic Probation, you may be placed on Academic Suspension. This is entered on your transcript and you must meet with the Dean’s Office to establish the conditions for returning to Fulbright. Suspensions typically last for one term or one academic year, and you may be suspended a maximum of two times. A third suspension will result in the cancellation of your enrolment in the program, and you must apply for re-admission, providing a letter that addresses the reasons for your suspensions and the measures you have taken to address those reasons. The re-admission decision is made by the Dean’s Office in consultation with faculty and staff.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 11]
situation. The Registrar's Office will be informed as a matter of record and follow-up. Three official warnings shall result in Disciplinary Action, constituting Academic Probation or Academic Suspension. 6.3 Academic Probation This is the second level of intervention. It is intended to make students aware that their academic performance puts them at risk of losing the opportunity to study at Fulbright, either temporarily (Suspension) or permanently (Dismissal). Students on Academic Warning who fail to meet all the requirements of their Learning Contract may require an additional Academic Progress Meeting and may be placed on Academic Probation, typically resulting in an updated Learning Contract. Academic Probation typically lasts for a term. 6.4 Academic Suspension A student on Academic Probation who fails to fulfill all the requirements of their Learning Contract may be placed on Academic Suspension. ### Question 63: How does the P/NP grade work?  
### Answer: 

The P/NP grade option allows students to take a total of 8 credits (typically 2 courses, 4 credits each) in one academic year on a Pass/No Pass basis. Students must complete a Petition to Elect Pass/No Pass Grade form and submit it to the Registrar’s Office before a specific deadline (4:00 PM on Friday Week 4 of the term). Once a student converts a course to P/NP, the grade option cannot be changed back. Pass/No Pass grades do not apply to core courses and cannot be used to count toward major/minor requirements. A grade of 'C-' or higher will be counted as a Pass, and these courses can be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses. Any grade below a 'C-' will be counted as a No Pass, and no credit is granted for this result. The NP grade will be shown on the Official Transcript, and courses with a NP grade cannot be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses. The Registrar’s Office is responsible for converting the final grade to P/NP after receiving the instructor's final grade submission at the end of the term.

### Question 64: How many courses can I take as P/NP at maximum and how will it contribute to the official transcript GPA?  
### Answer: 

A student can take a total of 8 credits (typically 2 courses, 4 credits each) on a Pass/No Pass basis. Pass/No Pass grades do not apply to core courses and cannot be used to count toward major/minor requirements. A grade of ‘C-’ or higher will be counted as a Pass, and courses graded with a Pass grade can be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses. Any grade below a ‘C-’ will be counted as a No Pass, and no credit is granted for this result. The NP grade will be shown on the Official Transcript, but courses with a NP grade cannot be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses. All courses for which a P/NP, I, W, or RP grade is awarded are excluded from the GPA calculation.

### Question 65: I've failed the GWP due to personal reasons so will it count toward the 144 maximum credits I can have?  
### Answer: 

The question of whether a failed course (in this case, the GWP) counts toward the maximum 144 credits a student can earn at Fulbright University Vietnam depends on how the university's credit policies handle failed courses. According to the provided context:

- **Failed Courses and Credits**: Failed courses (with grades of 'F' or 'NP') count toward the total attempted credits, but not toward the GPA calculation. This means that while the course is counted in terms of the number of credits attempted, it does not contribute positively to the student's GPA.

- **Maximum Credits**: The maximum number of credits a student can earn at Fulbright University Vietnam is 144 credits.

Given these points, a failed course (with an 'F' or 'NP' grade) will indeed count toward the total attempted credits, but it will not contribute to the 144 maximum credits in a way that would prevent the student from earning additional credits in other courses where they achieve a passing grade (D or higher for letter grades, or a Pass for P/NP options).

**Clarification**: The failed course will not add to the 144 credits in the sense that it does not contribute positively to the student's total earned credits. However, the attempted credits (including failed courses) are part of the total credits attempted, which is a different metric from the maximum credits a student can earn.

**Conclusion**: In summary, a failed course will count toward the total attempted credits but not toward the maximum 144 credits a student can earn. The student can still earn up to the maximum 144 credits by successfully completing other courses with passing grades. The failed course does not prevent the student from reaching the 144 credit milestone through other courses.

### Question 66: What and how do I get an Academic Warning?  
### Answer: 

An Academic Warning is usually the first level of intervention for students who are not making satisfactory progress toward their degree and/or who fall below a 2.0 GPA, or for other reasons such as failure of attendance, participation, citizenship, or academic integrity. To receive an Academic Warning, the Registrar’s Office sends out an Academic Warning notification. The student is then required to attend an Academic Progress Meeting during which a Learning Contract will be created with specific conditions tailored to the individual situation. The Registrar's Office will be informed as a matter of record and follow-up. Three official warnings shall result in Disciplinary Action, constituting Academic Probation or Academic Suspension.

### Question 67: How can I make reservations of rooms for personal usage?  
### Answer: 

To make reservations for rooms for personal usage, you typically need to contact the relevant department or office at your university. Here's a step-by-step guide on how to proceed:

1. **Identify the Office**: Determine which office or department handles room reservations at your university. This could be the housing office, residential life, or a specific department that manages student accommodations.

2. **Contact the Office**: Reach out to the office via phone, email, or in person. You might need to provide your student ID number and other personal information to verify your identity.

3. **Request Reservation**: Clearly state your intention to reserve a room for personal usage. Provide the dates and times you need the room, as well as the purpose of your reservation (e.g., study session, personal retreat, etc.).

4. **Check Availability**: Ask if the room you're interested in is available during your requested dates and times. Some universities may have a calendar or online system where you can check availability yourself.

5. **Make the Reservation**: If the room is available, the office will guide you through the reservation process. This might involve filling out a form, paying a fee (if applicable), and receiving a confirmation.

6. **Receive Confirmation**: Once your reservation is confirmed, you should receive a confirmation email or letter detailing the reservation, including the room number, dates, and any specific rules or guidelines.

7. **Follow Guidelines**: Be sure to familiarize yourself with any rules or guidelines provided by the university regarding the use of reserved rooms. This may include restrictions on noise, duration of stay, and cleaning expectations.

8. **Check-In and Check-Out**: Arrive at the reserved room on time and ensure you leave it in the same condition as you found it, or as per the university's expectations.

9. **Cancellation Policy**: Be aware of the university's cancellation policy in case you need to cancel your reservation. Some universities may have specific procedures for this.

10. **Feedback**: After your reservation, consider providing feedback to the office about your experience. This can help improve the service for future students.

If your university has an online portal for room reservations, you might also be able to make the reservation yourself after logging in with your student credentials. Always refer to your university's specific procedures, as they can vary significantly from one institution to another.

**Note**: If the reservation is for a group or an event, additional steps may be required, such as submitting a request form and possibly obtaining approval from a faculty member or department head.

**References**: The information provided above is based on general practices and does not reference specific documents or policies, as the procedures can vary widely between institutions. Always consult your university's official resources for the most accurate and up-to-date information.

### Question 68: Can you provide me with some courses suggestion to take to major in Math?  
### Answer: 

To major in Applied Mathematics, you should start with the foundation courses, which include Linear Algebra, Single Variable Calculus, Introduction to Statistics, and Multivariable Calculus. These courses provide a strong foundation in essential mathematical concepts. After completing the foundation courses, you should move on to the intermediate courses, which include Probability, Differential Equations, Discrete Mathematics, and Numerical Analysis. These courses will help you narrow your focus and explore specific areas of mathematics. For the advanced courses, you should choose from a variety of options such as Advanced Statistics, Statistical Learning, Stochastic Calculus, Numerical Analysis, Optimization, and Partial Differential Equations. These courses will help you shape your study path into one of the applied fields like Applied Statistics, Engineering Mathematics, or Data Science. Additionally, you should take at least 2 applied courses from other majors, such as Game Theory from Economics, Signal, Systems, and Control from Engineering, or Introduction to Machine Learning from Computer Science. A Pure Mathematics course like Abstract Algebra or Real Analysis is also required to provide essential abstract concepts and structures. Participation in research seminars is encouraged to understand faculty research and recent developments in mathematical research. Lastly, a capstone project can be completed in the last year of study, which involves a one-year long research project that contributes to the knowledge of mathematics or its applications. Remember to consult with an academic advisor for course selection and to ensure you meet all the requirements for the major.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Major Descriptions and Flowcharts_OfficialVersion.pdf, Page: 17]
of areas with applications in Mathematics: • Applied Statistics (Economics, Social Sciences, Mathematical Finance, Bioinformatics…) • Engineering Mathematics (Signal processing, Numerical simulation, Inverse problems…) • Data Science (Machine learning, Artificial intelligence …) Students will take at least 2 advanced courses. Consultation with an academic advisor is required for course selection. Sample Advanced Courses • Advanced Statistics • Statistical Learning • Stochastic Calculus • Numerical Analysis • Optimization • Partial Differential Equations Elective Applied courses: These are the courses from other majors that emphasize the applications of Mathematics. ### Question 70: I'm currently under a General Work Program for Experiential Learning but the company do not pay me in any form. How can I get the subsidy from Fulbright University?  
### Answer: 

Fulbright University Vietnam's Experiential Learning Program (ELP) offers students the opportunity to gain academic credit for their experiential learning experiences. However, the ELP does not provide financial subsidies or compensation for work done under the program. The ELP is designed to provide academic credit for experiences that contribute to a student's education, but it does not guarantee payment from the participating organizations.

To receive academic credit under the ELP, students must complete a certain number of credits (between 4 and 12) and have their experiences approved by their academic advisor and the relevant ELP stream (which could be within Academic Affairs, Career Services, or Center for Entrepreneurship and Innovation). The approval process ensures that the experience meets academic standards and contributes to the student's educational goals.

If you are not being paid for your work under the General Work Program for Experiential Learning, it is important to discuss this with your academic advisor and the ELP coordinator. They may be able to provide guidance on how to make the most of your experience for academic credit, but they cannot provide financial compensation.

For financial support, students typically rely on other sources such as scholarships, grants, part-time jobs, or financial aid provided by Fulbright University Vietnam. If you are facing financial difficulties, you should reach out to the Financial Aid Office at Fulbright University Vietnam to explore available options.

Remember that the ELP is about the learning experience and its integration into your academic curriculum, not about earning income. The university's standard operating procedures and academic regulations govern the ELP, and any adjustments to these policies would typically require a review and decision by the relevant university authorities.

For detailed information on the ELP, including how to apply for academic credit, you should refer to the official ELP page on the Fulbright One Stop portal, as mentioned in the provided context: https://onestop.fulbright.edu.vn/s/article/Experiential-Learning-Program

In summary, while the ELP can provide academic credit for your experiential learning, it does not provide financial subsidies or compensation for the work you do. You should discuss your situation with your academic advisor and the Financial Aid Office to explore other financial support options available to you.

### Question 71: Can you give me the process of making a Capstone for graduation?  
### Answer: 

The Capstone process for graduation typically involves two main phases: Capstone I and Capstone II. Here's a breakdown of the process:

**Capstone I:**

- **Initial Planning:** At the beginning of the semester, students meet with their advisors to set a regular meeting schedule and establish expectations for submissions with a timeline.
- **Research and Gathering:** Students actively conduct research, gathering and organizing the information or materials needed to realize their project. They may begin the initial stages of production, subject to their advisors' approval.
- **Midterm Submission:** Students submit a revised project proposal and/or research questions, initial close readings, field journal extracts (for research), and possibly first drafts or excerpts of creative writing.
- **Regular Updates:** Students provide regular updates to their advisors, including progress on their applied projects.

**Capstone II:**

- **Focus on Production:** In Capstone II, students focus more on the production phase, whether it's writing a thesis or realizing an applied project. They continue research in support of their final submission.
- **Midterm Submission:** Similar to Capstone I, students submit drafts of chapters, documentation of an applied project's progress, and a rough draft or outline of their thesis.
- **End-of-Term Submission:** At the end of Capstone II, students submit a completed written thesis or a finished applied project. This submission is a combination of various components, such as a literature review, sample chapters, introductions, and other materials as agreed upon with their advisors.
- **Capstone Presentation:** Students are highly encouraged to present their findings to the larger Fulbright community at the end of Capstone II. The presentation format can be decided between the student and their advisors and may include PowerPoint presentations, board presentations, or a combination of various media presentations.
- **Final Evaluation:** The Capstone culminates with a formal defense and a final evaluation by two readers. The format and length of projects are flexible within certain limits.

**Overall Process:**

The entire Capstone experience typically begins in the Fall with Capstone I and ends in the Spring with Capstone II. Students work closely with a primary advisor and, to a lesser extent, a secondary advisor. The goal is for students to demonstrate their ability to conduct independent research and produce a substantial project, which can be a written thesis or an applied project. The process is designed to provide students with the time and guidance necessary to carry out a long-term research project, and it is a unique opportunity at the undergraduate level.

**Note:** The specific requirements and expectations may vary depending on the institution and the particular program or major in which the student is enrolled. Always refer to the specific guidelines provided by your academic institution for the most accurate and detailed information.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>

### Question 73: How can I graduate with Honor or lie within the top GPA?  
### Answer: 

To graduate with honors or lie within the top GPA, you must complete a capstone project and have it graded as "Honors." Here's how you can achieve this:

1. **Complete the Capstone Project**: 
   - Apply for the capstone during the term prior to the first term of the capstone (Capstone I).
   - Ensure you have completed at least 80 credits of coursework before applying.
   - Work closely with an advisor to dive deeply into a topic of your interest, focusing on ethics, application of theory to methods, and communication of ideas.

2. **Maintain a High GPA**:
   - For Social Studies majors, maintain a 3.6 GPA throughout your senior year.
   - For Computer Science majors, maintain a 3.5 GPA throughout your senior year.
   - Adherence to these GPAs is crucial as failure to maintain the required GPA will result in the capstone being capped at "Pass," thus preventing you from graduating with honors.

3. **Quality of the Proposal**:
   - Ensure your capstone proposal is original, relevant, and methodologically sound.
   - It should demonstrate original thinking and be innovative within the social studies discipline.

4. **Evaluation and Grading**:
   - Your capstone project will be graded "No Pass/Pass/Honors."
   - It must be evaluated by your supervising faculty at least one month before the end of your graduating term.

5. **Advising and Support**:
   - Work with your primary advisor and secondary advisor to ensure your project aligns with your interests and expertise.
   - Your primary advisor will be the primary reviewer of your work.

6. **Eligibility**:
   - Fulfill all major requirements, including any additional requirements like military training for Vietnamese students.

By following these steps and maintaining the required GPA, you will have the opportunity to graduate with honors, which will reflect your academic excellence and dedication to your field of study.

[Source: Major Descriptions and Flowcharts_OfficialVersion.pdf, Page: 76]

### Question 74: How many courses can I take with P/NP grade in total?

### Question 75: How many types of absences are there?  
### Answer: 

There are three types of absences. The first type is general absences which include medical appointments, internship interviews, funerals, weddings, jury duty, etc. The second type is military leave, which is rare but can occur when a student is on-call duty and has military trainings or orders that conflict with the first weeks of class. The third type is excused absence due to university-sponsored events/activities for academic, non-academic, and recognized student organizations.

### Question 76: How many types of leave of absence are there and how can I have one?  
### Answer: 

There are three types of leave of absence: Personal Leave, Medical Leave, and Administrative Leave of Absence. To have one, you must complete and submit the Undergraduate Leave of Absence form, along with supporting documents if required, before the last day of class. For Personal Leave, you simply need to fill out the form. For Medical Leave, you must also submit the Fulbright Impact Assessment form and all medical supporting documents. For Administrative Leave of Absence, you may be placed on this leave if you have an outstanding student account balance without informing Student Financial Services to request a late and/or an extension of tuition fee payment. In this case, the Student Financial Services team will attempt to determine the circumstances and request a timely response from you. Please note that indefinite leaves are not permitted.

### Question 77: How can I report violation of Academic environment anonymously?  
### Answer: 

At Fulbright University Vietnam, if you wish to report a violation of the academic environment anonymously, you can do so by utilizing the anonymous reporting mechanisms provided by the university. While specific procedures may vary, here are general steps you might consider:

1. **Use the University's Reporting System**: Many universities have established anonymous reporting systems where students, faculty, or staff can report concerns or violations without revealing their identity. Check the university's website or One Stop portal for any available anonymous reporting tools.

2. **Contact the Office of Academic Affairs**: You can reach out to the Office of Academic Affairs directly, either through email or a phone call, to express your concerns. While this may not be entirely anonymous, the office may have protocols in place to protect your identity.

3. **Reach Out to the Dean's Office**: Similar to the Office of Academic Affairs, the Dean's Office may have mechanisms to handle reports of academic misconduct or violations in a confidential manner.

4. **Use University Hotlines**: Some universities have hotlines or dedicated phone numbers for reporting concerns or violations anonymously.

5. **Write a Letter**: If you prefer to write, you can draft a letter detailing the violation and send it to the appropriate office (e.g., Academic Affairs, Registrar's Office, Dean's Office) without signing your name.

6. **Consult the University's Policy**: Review the university's academic policy document for any specific instructions on how to report violations anonymously. The policy might outline a process for reporting concerns confidentially.

7. **Seek Advice from Trusted Advisors**: Before taking action, consider discussing your concerns with a trusted advisor, such as a counselor, academic advisor, or faculty member, who might offer guidance on how to proceed.

Remember, while anonymity can protect you from potential retaliation, it may also limit the ability of the university to fully investigate and address the issue. If you choose to report anonymously, be as specific as possible in your report to help the university understand the situation.

**Note**: The specific procedures and availability of anonymous reporting mechanisms can vary significantly from one institution to another. Always refer to the specific policies and procedures of Fulbright University Vietnam for the most accurate and relevant information.

It is important to keep track of these forms and documents as they are crucial for maintaining your academic status, registering for courses, and ensuring a smooth academic journey at Fulbright.

### Question 79: What is the school's policy on academic dishonesty, and how are violations handled?  
### Answer: 

The school's policy on academic dishonesty is outlined in the Code of Academic Integrity. Violations of academic integrity are taken seriously and are subject to intervention and disciplinary action. The process begins with an Academic Warning, which is usually the first level of intervention for students who are not making satisfactory progress toward their degree, falling below a 2.0 GPA, or for other reasons such as failure of attendance, participation, citizenship, or academic integrity. An Academic Warning is sent out by the Registrar’s Office, and the student is required to attend an Academic Progress Meeting where a Learning Contract is created with specific conditions tailored to the individual situation.

Three official warnings shall result in Disciplinary Action, constituting Academic Probation or Academic Suspension. Academic Probation is the second level of intervention, intended to make students aware that their academic performance puts them at risk of losing the opportunity to study at Fulbright, either temporarily (Suspension) or permanently (Dismissal). Students on Academic Warning who fail to meet all the requirements of their Learning Contract may be placed on Academic Probation, typically resulting in an updated Learning Contract.

Academic Suspension is the next step, where a student on Academic Probation who fails to fulfill all the requirements of their Learning Contract may be placed on Academic Suspension. Suspensions are entered on the student’s transcript as part of their academic record. The Registrar's Office will be informed as a matter of record and follow-up.

In addition to these academic interventions, the policy also addresses class attendance and absences. Students are encouraged to request permission to be absent at least 24 hours prior to class time and to make up any missed assignments if the absence is reasonable. A course withdrawal or an Incomplete grade may be pursued if appropriate under the University policies.

In summary, the school takes academic dishonesty very seriously and follows a structured process of intervention and disciplinary action, starting with an Academic Warning and potentially leading to Academic Probation or Suspension. Students are also expected to follow policies regarding class attendance and making up missed work.

### Question 80: What are the policies regarding retaking exams or improving grades?  
### Answer: 

Students are required to repeat core courses if they receive an F grade or a grade below 'C-' in courses that count toward their major or minor. They may also repeat a course if they received a grade of 'D+', 'D', 'F', or 'NP', or if they withdrew with a 'W'. In special cases, a student may request to repeat a course after receiving a grade higher than 'D+' following consultation with their academic/major advisor, the course instructor, and the Registrar’s Office. Considerations for repeating include course availability and capacity in the next academic term or year. The higher grade will be kept and used in the GPA calculation, while the lower grade will be overwritten with an 'RP' notation, meaning "repeated", and remain on the transcript. Credits of the repeated course are counted toward the total attempted credits. A student may not retake the same course for a third time unless they failed the second time or if a specific grade is needed to meet major requirements. Students should consult with their Academic/Major Advisor before taking a course for a third time.

The policy also states that a higher grade will replace a lower grade in the GPA calculation, and the lower grade will be marked with an 'RP' notation on the transcript. The repeated course's credits will count toward the total attempted credits. However, students are not allowed to retake the same course for a third time unless they failed the second attempt or a specific grade is required for their major.

Regarding withdrawals, a student may withdraw from a course without penalty to their GPA up until the end of Week 4 for an 8-week course or Week 8 for a full-term course. After this point, a withdrawal results in an 'F' grade, which will affect the GPA. Exceptions to this policy require exceptional circumstances, supported by documentation, and must be authorized by the course instructor(s), the student's academic/major advisor, and the Registrar’s Office.

In the case of an 'Incomplete' grade ('I'), it may be awarded if a student is unable to complete the course requirements due to illness, family emergency, or other exceptional circumstances. The student has up to 6 months from the end of the course to complete the remaining work, after which they will receive a letter grade, possibly an 'F', based on the work completed by the deadline. An Incomplete Grade Request form must be submitted to the Registrar’s Office by the last day of the term end date.

In summary, students may retake courses to improve their grades, but there are specific rules and limitations in place. They must consult with their advisors and the Registrar’s Office, and they cannot retake a course for a third time without a valid reason. Withdrawals can be made without GPA impact up until a certain point in the term, after which an 'F' grade will be assigned. An 'Incomplete' grade may be awarded under certain circumstances, with a deadline for completion set by the faculty member and the Registrar’s Office.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]

A higher grade will be kept and used in the GPA calculation. The lower grade will be overwritten by the notation “RP”, meaning “repeated”, and remain on the transcript. Credits of the repeated course are counted toward the total attempted credits. A student may not retake the same course for the third time unless he/she failed the second time or if a specific grade is needed to meet the major requirements. Students may repeat a course if they have received a grade of ‘D+’, ‘D’, ‘F’, or NP for the course or have withdrawn and received a grade of ‘W’. In special cases, a student may request to repeat a course after having received a grade higher than a ‘D+’ following consultation with the student’s academic/major advisor, the course instructor, and the Registrar’s Office. Considerations will include course availability and capacity in the next academic term or next academic year. A higher grade will be kept and used in the GPA calculation. The lower grade will be overwritten by the notation “RP”, meaning “repeated”, and remain on the transcript. Credits of the repeated course are counted toward the total attempted credits. A student may not retake the same course for the third time unless he/she failed

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 7]

A student who withdraws from a course beyond the halfway point of that course (end of week 4 for an 8-week course or end of week 8 for a full-term course) automatically receives a grade of ‘F’, which will affect the student’s GPA. ### Question 81: How does the university accommodate students with chronic illnesses or personal emergencies that affect attendance?  
### Answer: 

The university acknowledges that students may experience exceptional circumstances, such as exceptional medical circumstances (including chronic illnesses), close bereavement, being a victim of a serious crime, disabilities for which reasonable adjustments are not yet in place, exceptional and unforeseeable transport difficulties, legal proceedings requiring attendance, military leave, and university-sponsored events. In such cases, students are expected to inform their instructors as soon as possible and provide appropriate documentation. Instructors are responsible for outlining attendance expectations and communicating consequences of unexcused absences. They are also expected to allow students to make up missed assignments if the absence is reasonable.

For chronic illnesses or ongoing medical conditions, students may need to provide documentation from a health services professional verifying their impact on the student's ability to attend class, perform sustained reading, note-taking, and writing, and engage in tasks requiring intense concentration. The university encourages instructors to accommodate students in these situations.

In cases of personal emergencies, students should also inform their instructors and provide appropriate documentation. The university encourages flexibility and understanding from instructors in these situations.

For students with chronic illnesses or personal emergencies that significantly affect their ability to attend classes, the university may consider a voluntary medical leave of absence. This involves submitting an Undergraduate Leave of Absence form, along with medical supporting documents, before the last day of class. The leave duration is determined in conjunction with health services professionals, the Registrar's Office, and the student.

It's important to note that indefinite leaves are not permitted, and students must be in good academic standing to be considered for an excused absence. The university encourages students to communicate openly with their instructors and to seek support from the Office of the Dean and Deans of Students for approval of extended absences related to university-sponsored events or activities.

In summary, the university accommodates students with chronic illnesses or personal emergencies by allowing excused absences, enabling students to make up missed work, and considering a voluntary medical leave of absence if necessary. Students are responsible for communicating their situations to their instructors and providing appropriate documentation. Instructors are expected to be flexible and accommodating within the framework of university policies.

### Question 82: Are students allowed to use AI tools like ChatGPT for assignments? If so, under what conditions?  
### Answer: 

Students are allowed to use AI tools like ChatGPT for their assignments, but under specific conditions. Firstly, they must adhere to Fulbright University Vietnam’s Code of Academic Integrity, which includes regulations on the usage of generative AI. This means that creative projects involving generative AI require full documentation of its usage. The documentation must include:

1. **Objective and Scope**: Clearly define the reasons for utilizing generative AI and the specific elements of the project it contributes to.
2. **Tools and Platforms**: Specify the AI tools, models, or platforms employed.
3. **Process and Methodology**: Outline how AI will be incorporated, detailing which aspects of the project will be generated, improved, or altered with the use of AI.
4. **Ethical and Copyright Issues**: Address the ethical and copyright concerns associated with using generative AI and how these will be addressed throughout the project.

This comprehensive documentation is crucial as it promotes transparency, offers insight into AI's role in the creative process, and highlights the originality and human contributions to the project. Furthermore, students must obtain approval from Fulbright University Vietnam’s Institutional Review Board (IRB) before starting their research, especially if it involves data collection. The IRB approval process involves taking an online module to learn about IRB procedures and submitting an application detailing the research design and plan for data protection.

In summary, while students are allowed to use AI tools like ChatGPT, they must ensure full documentation of its usage and adhere to the IRB approval process for research involving data collection. Failure to comply with these conditions could result in delays to the project and/or its suspension.

### Question 83: Where can I get support for mental health treatment?  
### Answer: 

The Resource Guide for Local Mental Health Services is a crucial document that can provide comprehensive support for mental health treatment. This guide typically includes detailed listings of local mental health professionals, clinics, and community resources. It may also offer information on the types of services available, such as counseling, therapy, support groups, and emergency services. The guide is designed to help individuals and families navigate the mental health care system and access the appropriate services they need.

The Capstone by Applied Project, which could include the development of such a guide, requires extensive documentation of the process through which the original work was developed. This includes identifying community needs through a Community Survey on Mental Health Needs, consulting with mental health practitioners, and collaborating with local organizations to ensure the accuracy and relevance of the information provided.

In addition to the guide, students working on a Capstone project related to mental health services might also benefit from the support of a Non-Academic Advisor, such as a mental health practitioner, who can provide expert insights and guidance throughout the project.

Furthermore, the Evaluation Report for the Capstone project must demonstrate the project’s relevance to psychological principles, its potential or observed impact, and evidence of rigorous evaluation. This report should also include documentation of the student’s involvement and implementation of the program, as well as insights or recommendations for future application or research.

Logistical support for the project, such as organizing events or exhibitions related to mental health, can be arranged through the university, ensuring that all necessary precautions are taken to protect the student and the institution from liability concerns.

In summary, for support in mental health treatment, one should refer to the Resource Guide for Local Mental Health Services, which can be developed through a comprehensive Capstone project that involves community engagement, expert consultation, and rigorous evaluation. Support for the project can be obtained through academic and non-academic advisors, and logistical support can be arranged through the university to ensure the project's success and safety.

### Question 84: Where can I get the information about motorcycle parking?  
### Answer: 

The information about motorcycle parking can typically be found through the following resources:

1. **Official Website of the Municipality or City**: Most cities have an official website where they provide detailed maps and regulations regarding parking, including designated areas for motorcycles.

2. **Local Government Offices**: Visiting or contacting local government offices, such as the city planning department or the parking authority, can provide direct and up-to-date information.

3. **Local Police Stations**: Police stations may have information about parking regulations, including motorcycle parking, and can also provide advice on where to park legally and safely.

4. **Community Centers or Libraries**: These institutions often have maps and resources that include parking information, and librarians or community center staff may be able to assist.

5. **Neighborhood Associations**: If you are part of a neighborhood association, they may have local knowledge about parking spots and regulations.

6. **Online Maps and Apps**: Many online mapping services and apps offer parking information, including designated motorcycle parking spots. Services like Google Maps, Waze, or city-specific apps may have this information.

7. **Local Business Owners**: Speaking to local business owners can sometimes yield useful information about parking in the area, including motorcycle parking.

8. **University or Workplace**: If you are affiliated with a university or workplace, they may have specific parking policies and information available.

9. **Signage and Street Markings**: On-site signage and street markings often indicate designated motorcycle parking areas.

10. **Local News and Community Bulletins**: Sometimes local news outlets or community bulletins will publish information about changes to parking regulations.

When seeking information about motorcycle parking, it's important to verify the accuracy of the information and to be aware of any changes in parking regulations that might have occurred since the last update of the resource. Always follow local laws and regulations regarding parking to avoid fines or towing.

### Question 85: Where can I find resources to facilitate my graduate program after Fulbright undergraduate?  
### Answer: 

For resources to facilitate your graduate program after completing your undergraduate studies at Fulbright University Vietnam, you should start by utilizing the university's own resources and services. Here are some steps and resources you might consider:

1. **Career Services (CS)**: Fulbright University Vietnam has a dedicated Career Services department that can provide guidance on graduate school applications, including resume building, personal statement writing, and interview preparation. They may also have a database of graduate programs and scholarships.

2. **Academic Advising**: Your primary advisor or the academic advising office can offer advice on graduate studies, help you identify relevant programs, and provide letters of recommendation if needed.

3. **Experiential Learning Program (ELP)**: The ELP can be a valuable resource for gaining practical experience that might strengthen your graduate school application. The ELP can also provide opportunities for networking with professionals in various fields.

4. **Center for Entrepreneurship and Innovation (CEI)**: If you're interested in entrepreneurship or innovation-related graduate programs, the CEI can offer support, mentorship, and resources.

5. **Library and Research Services**: The Fulbright University library and research services can help you find academic journals, books, and other resources relevant to your graduate studies interests.

6. **Alumni Network**: Fulbright University Vietnam has an alumni network that can be a valuable resource for finding mentors, learning about graduate programs, and gaining insights into the application process.

7. **Online Resources**: Utilize online platforms such as GradSchools.com, Peterson's, and individual university websites to research graduate programs, requirements, and application processes.

8. **Workshops and Seminars**: Attend any workshops or seminars hosted by Fulbright University or external organizations that focus on graduate school preparation.

9. **Financial Aid Office**: If you're concerned about the financial aspect of graduate studies, the financial aid office can provide information on scholarships, fellowships, and loans.

10. **OneStop**: Fulbright University's OneStop portal may have specific resources or guides related to post-graduate planning.

For detailed information on the Experiential Learning Program (ELP), you can refer to the official Fulbright University Vietnam website here: https://onestop.fulbright.edu.vn/s/article/Experiential-Learning-Program

Remember to start planning early and maintain regular contact with the relevant departments and offices at Fulbright University Vietnam to ensure you're making the most of the resources available to you.

### Question 86: Can you give me information about teaching assistant program right now?  
### Answer: 

Teaching assistantships are not specifically mentioned in the provided contexts. However, based on the general information provided about the Computer Science major and the Social Studies Capstone, we can infer some general principles that might apply to teaching assistant programs:

2. **Allocation of Advisor Process**: Similar to the allocation of advisors for capstone projects, the selection process for teaching assistants might involve faculty review and selection based on academic performance, interest in teaching, and other relevant criteria.

3. **Advising Process**: Students interested in becoming teaching assistants would likely go through an advising process where they discuss their qualifications, responsibilities, and expectations with a faculty member.

4. **Capstone Experience**: Given the emphasis on active and collaborative learning in the Computer Science major, teaching assistants might be involved in supporting and facilitating capstone projects, thereby gaining hands-on teaching experience.

5. **IRB Approval**: If the teaching assistantship involves research or human subjects, the process would require IRB approval, similar to capstone projects.

6. **Academic Integrity**: Teaching assistants would be expected to uphold the highest standards of academic integrity, just as they would in their own studies.

7. **Grading Process**: Teaching assistants might be involved in the grading process for courses, under the supervision of faculty members.

8. **Group Project**: As teaching assistants, students might be involved in organizing and supporting group projects, which would be beneficial for their own learning and development.

9. **Dissemination**: Teaching assistants might also be involved in the dissemination of course materials, research findings, or best practices in teaching and learning.

### Question 88: How can I get the information of campus usage for events so that I can have proper place to study without getting interrupted?  
### Answer: 

To get information about campus usage for events, you should contact the campus events office or the office of student activities. They typically maintain a calendar of events and can provide you with information about scheduled events and the availability of spaces for study. Here are some steps you can take:

1. Visit the university's website: Often, universities have a calendar of events or a schedule of classes and events that can be accessed online. This can give you an overview of what's happening on campus.

2. Contact the campus events office: Reach out to the office responsible for scheduling events on campus. They can provide you with a calendar or inform you about upcoming events and the availability of study spaces.

3. Check with the library: Libraries often have quiet study areas and may have information about events that could impact study space availability.

4. Talk to your academic advisor: Advisors are familiar with the campus and can provide guidance on where to study and when to avoid certain areas due to events.

5. Use campus maps: Some universities provide maps that indicate where events are taking place, which can help you plan your study schedule.

6. Sign up for event notifications: Many universities offer email notifications for events. Signing up for these can keep you informed and help you plan your study schedule accordingly.

7. Visit in person: If possible, visit the campus events office in person to discuss your needs and inquire about study spaces.

By following these steps, you should be able to gather the necessary information to plan your study schedule effectively and avoid being interrupted by campus events. Remember to also check the university's policies on studying in different areas, as some spaces may have restrictions during events.

### Question 89: I used to take an undergraduate program at another university and I want to transfer credit of studied courses at that university. What should I do?  
### Answer: 

When applying for Credit Transfer, a student is responsible for providing all the information that is requested about the course(s) for which they are applying to transfer. Information may include but not limited to course curriculum, learning outcomes, course content, and assessments. To apply for Credit Transfer or an Exemption, students should submit an Application for Credit Transfer, along with the required information on the course(s), to the Office of the Registrar. The Registrar will coordinate with the Office of the Dean to determine whether credit or an exemption is justified.

### Question 90: What are the policies of CWP?  
### Answer: 

The policies of CWP (Capstone Writing Project) at Fulbright University Vietnam are outlined in the provided context. Here are the key points:

1. **University-wide Application**: The policy applies to the entire university, but majors and minors may have additional requirements which are clearly stated in their respective descriptions and handbooks.

2. **Approval Process**: Any exception to the policy must be approved by the major coordinator and the Dean’s Office.

3. **Regular Updates**: The document is subject to regular updates as the university grows and evolves, with a commitment to innovation and continuous improvement.

4. **Capstone Project Requirements**:
   - **Advisory Consultation**: Students are encouraged to consult early with their prospective advisors about the capstone project.
   - **Project Approval**: Applications for the capstone project must demonstrate an understanding of the scope and practicalities involved. Projects without current faculty expertise may not be approved.
   - **GPA Requirement**: To earn Honors for the capstone, students must maintain a 3.6 GPA throughout their senior year. Failure to maintain this GPA will result in the capstone being capped at Pass.

5. **Logistical Support**:
   - **Advance Notification**: For projects requiring logistical arrangements outside the university’s typical academic scope, students must notify the relevant faculty and university functionaries well in advance.
   - This includes events organized in partnership with external groups, applied projects on campus, and any project that may raise liability concerns.

6. **Capstone Writing Project Evaluation Criteria**:
   - **Concept**: The central idea, message, and story must be compelling, original, and innovative, drawing connections to literary and theoretical works and society.
   - **Process and Documentation**: The project must adhere to the agreed-upon schedule, and the process of creating the text(s) must be comprehensively documented.

The context does not specify a "CWP" directly, but it does outline the policies and procedures for the capstone writing project, which is likely what "CWP" refers to in the question. The policies are designed to ensure that students have support, standards, and flexibility while working on their capstone projects, and to maintain academic integrity and quality within the university's program.

### Question 91: I'm a student athlete then how can I bypass all of physical education courses required to graduate?  
### Answer: 

As a student athlete, you can bypass the physical education courses required to graduate by taking advantage of the special considerations often afforded to student athletes. Here are some steps you might consider:

1. **Consult with your Athletic Department:** Reach out to your athletic department or coach to discuss your academic requirements and how they might accommodate your athletic commitments. They may have established protocols for student athletes to bypass certain courses.

2. **Talk to your Academic Advisor:** Your academic advisor can help navigate the university's policies and procedures regarding course exemptions. They can guide you on how to petition for an exemption from physical education courses based on your athletic commitments.

3. **Petition Process:** Many universities have a formal petition process for students to request exemptions from certain requirements. Your academic advisor can guide you through this process, which typically involves submitting a written request detailing your circumstances and why you should be exempted from the physical education requirement.

4. **Document Your Commitments:** To strengthen your case for exemption, gather documentation that demonstrates your commitment to your sport, such as your athletic schedule, letters from coaches, and any awards or recognitions you've received.

5. **Understand University Policies:** Familiarize yourself with your university's policies regarding course exemptions for student athletes. Some institutions may have specific policies in place that automatically exempt student athletes from physical education courses.

6. **Consider Alternative Options:** If you cannot bypass the requirement entirely, explore alternative options such as online physical education courses or courses that can be completed during the summer or off-season.

7. **Maintain Good Academic Standing:** While pursuing this exemption, ensure you maintain a strong academic record to avoid any negative impacts on your athletic eligibility.

By following these steps and working closely with your academic advisor and athletic department, you can navigate the process of bypassing physical education courses required for graduation as a student athlete. Remember, each university may have different policies and procedures, so it's important to understand and follow your institution's specific guidelines.

For example, an exploratory course can also be counted as a major course for the corresponding major. However, the number of double-counted credits is often limited (e.g., see subsections 13.2 and 13.3). Additionally, any particular course can only be used to satisfy at most two requirements. For instance, if course X is cross-listed between major A and major B and tagged by minor C, then X can be used to fulfill the requirements of major A and major B, or major A and minor C, or major B and minor C. Triple counting is not allowed. 13.9  Maximal Length of Study Fulbright follows MOET regulations, which state that the maximum time to complete the program cannot exceed double the standard

### Question 92: I'm currently a third year student and moved out of university dormitory after first year but now I'm struggling to find a new accommodation so can I register again for dormitory and will I still have the financial support?  
### Answer: 

Students cannot register for courses in the forthcoming term if they are not in “Active” status and/or have an outstanding financial balance on their account. If you are currently on a Leave of Absence due to financial reasons, you will need to clear your outstanding balance before you can be reinstated to "Active" status. You should meet with the Student Financial Services team as soon as possible to request assistance and alternative solutions. Regarding the university dormitory, you would need to contact the Residential Life office to inquire about availability and the process to move back into the dormitory. Financial support for accommodation may vary depending on the university's policies and any available scholarships or bursaries. It is best to check with the Financial Aid office to see if there are any options available to you given your current situation. Keep in mind that being on a Leave of Absence does not necessarily mean you are ineligible for future financial support; however, you will need to discuss your situation with the relevant offices to explore your options.

### Question 93: Can you give me the procedure to request for funds to support club activities?  
### Answer: 

To request funds to support club activities at Fulbright University Vietnam (FUV), follow these steps:

1. **Identify the Need**: Clearly define the purpose and scope of the club activity that requires funding. This includes the budget breakdown, expected outcomes, and how the activity aligns with the club's goals and FUV's mission.

2. **Research Available Funding Sources**: Check with FUV's administration or the Office of Student Affairs to understand the available funding options. FUV might have specific funds designated for student clubs and activities.

3. **Prepare a Proposal**: Develop a detailed proposal outlining the club activity, its objectives, expected outcomes, budget, and how the funds will be utilized. Include a timeline for the activity and any other relevant information.

4. **Consult with Advisors**: Before submitting the proposal, consult with your club advisors, faculty members, or mentors to get feedback and suggestions on how to strengthen your proposal.

5. **Submit the Proposal**: Submit your proposal to the designated office or person responsible for approving club funding requests. This could be the Office of Student Affairs, the Dean's Office, or another relevant department.

6. **Follow Up**: After submission, follow up to ensure your proposal is being reviewed and to address any questions or concerns that may arise.

7. **Approval and Disbursement**: If your proposal is approved, you will receive the funds according to the terms and conditions set by FUV. Ensure you adhere to all guidelines regarding the use of the funds.

8. **Reporting and Accountability**: After the club activity is completed, prepare a report detailing how the funds were used, the outcomes of the activity, and any lessons learned. This report may be required for accountability purposes.

9. **Thank and Acknowledge**: Always thank the funding sources and acknowledge their support in any related communications, reports, or promotional materials.

It's important to note that the specific procedures and requirements may vary, so it's best to consult directly with FUV's administration or the Office of Student Affairs for the most accurate and up-to-date information. Additionally, maintaining open communication with the funding body and adhering to all guidelines and deadlines is crucial to ensure a smooth process and successful club activity.

### Question 94: How many ways are there provided by the university can I get the support in my academic path?  
### Answer: 

There are several ways the university provides support in the academic path of students. Firstly, students have access to labs, tools, and software relevant to their project work, which is crucial for practical learning and application. Secondly, support is provided for learning new software or techniques where necessary, ensuring that students are not left behind in terms of technological advancements and skills development. Thirdly, mentorship and industry involvement are available, with industry mentors potentially serving as secondary advisors for Capstone projects or joining the capstone panel to provide industry insights and guidance. This helps bridge the gap between academic learning and real-world practice. Fourthly, funding and material procurement policies are in place, allowing students access to limited funding for materials and resources needed for their projects. Lastly, the university acknowledges exceptional circumstances that may impact a student's ability to fulfill academic expectations, providing support and accommodations for issues such as medical circumstances, bereavement, disabilities, and unforeseeable transport difficulties. This comprehensive support system is designed to ensure that students have the resources and assistance they need to succeed in their academic and project work.
